Division of Conflicting Claims: Munaza'a vs 'Awl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division method for conflicting claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi methods of munaza'a and 'awl to divide property between claimants with unequal claims and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Unequal claims require proportional division: Abu Hanifa gives three-quarters, Sahibayn give two-thirds.

When two claimants present equal evidence for different shares of a house, the Hanafi school has two methods of division. Abu Hanifa uses 'munaza'a' (giving the uncontested half first, then splitting the contested part). The Sahibayn use 'awl' (proportional reduction, treating claims as shares in a partnership). Understanding the difference reveals how legal principles shape outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claims
Note that one claimant claims half the house, the other claims the whole house. Both present equally strong evidence.
The house is in the hand of a third party (possession not part of claim).
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's method (munaza'a)
Determine the uncontested portion: the half-claimant does not contest the other half, so that half goes to the whole-claimant. The remaining half is contested equally, so each gets half of that quarter. Result: whole-claimant gets 3/4, half-claimant gets 1/4.
Think of it as two steps: uncontested part first, then equal division of the contested remainder.
3
Apply the Sahibayn's method ('awl/mudaraba)
Treat each claim as a capital contribution. The whole-claimant's claim is twice as strong as the half-claimant's. Divide the whole into three shares (two for the whole, one for the half). Result: whole-claimant gets 2/3, half-claimant gets 1/3.
This is analogous to inheritance 'awl or partnership sharing.
4
Compare and evaluate
Note the practical difference: 3/4 vs 2/3 for the whole-claimant. The later Hanafi authorities (mufta bihi) prefer the Sahibayn's view as more systematic.
This is an intra-madhhab difference; both are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (دار) في يد آخر ادعى رجل نصفها وآخر كلها وبرهنا فللأول ربعها والباقي للآخر) عند أبي حنيفة اعتباراً لطريق المنازعة فإن صاحب النصف لا ينازع الآخر النصف في سلم له واستوت منازعتهما في النصف الآخر فينتصف بينهما. وقالا : بينهما أثلاثاً فاعتبر طريق العول والمضاربة فصاحب الجميع يضرب بكل حقه سهمين وصاحب النصف بسهم واحد فيقسم أثلاثاً. وذكر في الهداية أن لهذه المسألة نظائر وأضداداً لا يحتملها هذا المختصر وقد ذكرناها في الزيادات اهـ. وذكر المؤلف في الكافي بعضها وقال: وسيجيء في كتاب الديات على الاستقصاء مع الأصول إن شاء الله تعالى .اهـ. وفي المبسوط ما يخالفه كما علم من الكافي وفيه : دار في يد زيد برهن عمرو على أنه باعها من بكر بألف وبرهن بكر على أنه باعها من عمرو بمائة دينار وجحد زيد ذلك كله قضى بالدار بين المدعيين ولا يقضى بشيء من الثمنين لأنه تعذر القضاء بالبيع لجهالة التاريخ. ولم يتعذر القضاء بالملك، وعند محمد يقضى بها بينهما ولكل واحد نصف الثمن على صاحبه لأنه لم يسلم لكل واحد إلا نصف المبيع. ولو ادعت امرأة شراء الدار من عمرو بألف وعمرو ادعى أنه اشتراها منها بألف وزيد وهو ذو اليد يدعي أنها له اشتراها من عمرو بألف وأقاموا البينة قضى لذي اليد لتعارض بينتي غيره فبقيت بينته بلا معارض. وعند محمد يقضى بالدار لذي اليد بألف عليه للخارج ويقضى لها على الخارج بألف لأن ذا اليد والمرأة ادعيا التلقي من الخارج فيجعل كأنها في يده اهـ. وقيد بقوله «ولا تاريخ لأنهما لو أرخا يقضى به لصاحب الوقت الآخر؛ كذا في خزانة الأكمل. وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أنه لو برهن كل على إقرار الآخر أن هذا الشيء له فإنهما يتهاتران ويبقى في يد ذي اليد ؛ كذا في الخزانة أيضاً قوله : ( ولا يرجح بزيادة عدد الشهود) فلو أقام أحد المدعيين شاهدين والآخر أربعة فهما سواء، وكذا لا ترجيح بزيادة العدالة لأن الترجيح يقع بكثرة العلل حتى لا يترجح القياس بقياس آخر ولا الحديث بحديث آخر، وشهادة كل شاهدين علة تامة فلا تصلح للترجيح والعدالة ليست بذي حد فلا يقع الترجيح بها .
His statement: (A house) in the hand of another, a man claimed half of it and another claimed all of it, and they presented evidence, then for the first is one quarter and the rest is for the other according to Abu Hanifa, considering the method of opposition: the one claiming half does not contest the other regarding half, so it is surrendered to him, and their opposition is equal in the other half, so it is divided equally between them. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is divided into thirds between them, considering the method of 'awl and mudaraba: the one claiming all enters with his full right (two shares) and the one claiming half enters with one share, so it is divided into thirds. It is mentioned in al-Hidayah that this issue has parallels and opposites that this abridgement cannot contain, and we have mentioned them in al-Ziyadat. And the author mentioned some of them in al-Kafi and said: 'And it will come in the Book of Diyat with full discussion of principles, God willing.' In al-Mabsut there is something contradicting this, as known from al-Kafi. Therein: A house in the hand of Zayd; 'Amr presented evidence that he sold it to Bakr for a thousand, and Bakr presented evidence that he sold it to 'Amr for a hundred dinars, and Zayd denied all of that; the house is judged to be between the two claimants and nothing is judged of the two prices because judging the sale is impossible due to ignorance of the date, but judging ownership is not impossible. According to Muhammad, it is judged to be between them, and each one gets half the price from his companion because only half of the sold property is delivered to each. And if a woman claimed she bought the house from 'Amr for a thousand, and 'Amr claimed that he bought it from her for a thousand, and Zayd, the possessor, claimed it is his, having bought it from 'Amr for a thousand, and they presented evidence, judgment is for the possessor because the evidence of the others conflict, so his evidence remains without opponent. According to Muhammad, the house is judged to be for the possessor with a thousand owed to the outsider, and he judges that she owes a thousand to the outsider because the possessor and the woman both claim receipt from the outsider, so it is as if it is in his hand. And he restricted by his statement 'and no date' because if they dated, judgment would be for the one with the later time; as in Khizanat al-Akmal. And the author indicated that if each presented evidence of the other's admission that this thing is his, then they cancel each other out and it remains in the hand of the possessor; as in al-Khazanah also. His statement: 'And preference is not given by an increase in the number of witnesses.' So if one of the two claimants brings two witnesses and the other brings four, they are equal. Likewise, no preference is given by an increase in probity because preference occurs by abundance of effective causes; so a qiyas is not preferred over another qiyas, nor a hadith over another hadith. The testimony of each pair of witnesses is a complete cause, so it is not suitable for preference, and probity has no defined limit, so preference does not occur by it.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the division of a house when two claimants present equal evidence, one claiming half and the other the whole. It opens with the ruling of Abu Hanifa: he divides by way of 'munaza'a' (opposition/confrontation). The claimant of half already has half uncontested, so he gets that half, and the remaining half is contested equally, so each gets half of that, resulting in three-quarters for the claimant of the whole and one-quarter for the claimant of half. The two Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, divide by way of 'awl and mudaraba' (proportional reduction and partnership). They see the dispute as similar to a partnership where each partner contributes his share of the claim. The claimant of the whole has a right of two shares (since he claims the entire house, which is twice the other's claim), and the claimant of half has one share, so the house is divided into three parts: the claimant of the whole gets two-thirds, the claimant of half gets one-third. The author then notes that this case has parallels and opposites detailed in al-Ziyadat and al-Kafi. Several other scenarios are given: a complicated triple claim involving a house, a woman's claim, and a possessor's claim, with differences between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The section ends with the rule that the number of witnesses does not tip the balance when evidence conflicts, as each pair of witnesses constitutes a complete cause (illah).

Key Terms
المنازعة (al-munaza'a): Method of giving each claimant what is not contested by the other, then dividing the contested portion equally.
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of shares; here used to divide property in proportion to the strength of claims.
المضاربة (al-mudaraba): Partnership; in this context, each claimant's claim is treated as capital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, how is the house divided when one claims half and the other claims the whole?
A) Half-claimant gets 1/4, whole-claimant gets 3/4.
B) Half-claimant gets 1/3, whole-claimant gets 2/3.
C) Each gets half.
D) The whole-claimant gets the entire house.

Key Takeaway
When claims conflict with equal evidence, Hanafi jurists differ: Abu Hanifa uses munaza'a (3/4 vs 1/4), Sahibayn use 'awl (2/3 vs 1/3), with the latter being mufta bihi.

Witness Numbers Do Not Tip the Balance
Rule on preferring witnesses in conflicting claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an increase in the number or probity of witnesses does not give preference in conflicting evidence according to the Hanafi school, and identify the exception for dated evidence.

Core Idea
Each pair of witnesses is a complete legal cause; more witnesses do not override another's evidence.

In Hanafi judicial procedure, when two sets of witnesses give contradictory evidence, the qadi does not prefer the side with more witnesses or more pious witnesses. This is because the testimony of two witnesses constitutes a complete proof (hujja). Additional witnesses merely reinforce but do not create a stronger cause. The passage also notes an exception: if witnesses provide dates, the later transaction prevails.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle
The Hanafi rule: shahada (testimony) of two witnesses is a complete cause (illah tammah). Two witnesses create legal certainty. Adding more witnesses does not increase the certainty because it is already at its maximum.
This is different from some other schools that consider the number of witnesses.
2
Apply to conflicting testimony
If claimant A brings 2 witnesses, and claimant B brings 4 witnesses, both sets produce complete proof. Since both are equally conclusive, the qadi cannot prefer one over the other by number. The same applies to probity (adala): it has no defined threshold to create preference.
The text says 'al-tarjih occurs by multiplication of causes, not by number of witnesses.'
3
Identify the exception
If the witnesses provide dates (tariq), then the later dated evidence prevails because it suggests a later transfer of ownership. Without dates, the evidence is treated as equal.
Dates break the tie because they allow temporal ordering.
4
Contrast with other scenarios
In the triple claim scenario (woman, Amr, Zayd), the possessor's evidence prevails because the other two cancel each other out. This is not about witness number but about the effect of possession.
The rule about witnesses applies only when both sides present valid evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (دار) في يد آخر ادعى رجل نصفها وآخر كلها وبرهنا فللأول ربعها والباقي للآخر) عند أبي حنيفة اعتباراً لطريق المنازعة فإن صاحب النصف لا ينازع الآخر النصف في سلم له واستوت منازعتهما في النصف الآخر فينتصف بينهما. وقالا : بينهما أثلاثاً فاعتبر طريق العول والمضاربة فصاحب الجميع يضرب بكل حقه سهمين وصاحب النصف بسهم واحد فيقسم أثلاثاً. وذكر في الهداية أن لهذه المسألة نظائر وأضداداً لا يحتملها هذا المختصر وقد ذكرناها في الزيادات اهـ. وذكر المؤلف في الكافي بعضها وقال: وسيجيء في كتاب الديات على الاستقصاء مع الأصول إن شاء الله تعالى .اهـ. وفي المبسوط ما يخالفه كما علم من الكافي وفيه : دار في يد زيد برهن عمرو على أنه باعها من بكر بألف وبرهن بكر على أنه باعها من عمرو بمائة دينار وجحد زيد ذلك كله قضى بالدار بين المدعيين ولا يقضى بشيء من الثمنين لأنه تعذر القضاء بالبيع لجهالة التاريخ. ولم يتعذر القضاء بالملك، وعند محمد يقضى بها بينهما ولكل واحد نصف الثمن على صاحبه لأنه لم يسلم لكل واحد إلا نصف المبيع. ولو ادعت امرأة شراء الدار من عمرو بألف وعمرو ادعى أنه اشتراها منها بألف وزيد وهو ذو اليد يدعي أنها له اشتراها من عمرو بألف وأقاموا البينة قضى لذي اليد لتعارض بينتي غيره فبقيت بينته بلا معارض. وعند محمد يقضى بالدار لذي اليد بألف عليه للخارج ويقضى لها على الخارج بألف لأن ذا اليد والمرأة ادعيا التلقي من الخارج فيجعل كأنها في يده اهـ. وقيد بقوله «ولا تاريخ لأنهما لو أرخا يقضى به لصاحب الوقت الآخر؛ كذا في خزانة الأكمل. وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أنه لو برهن كل على إقرار الآخر أن هذا الشيء له فإنهما يتهاتران ويبقى في يد ذي اليد ؛ كذا في الخزانة أيضاً قوله : ( ولا يرجح بزيادة عدد الشهود) فلو أقام أحد المدعيين شاهدين والآخر أربعة فهما سواء، وكذا لا ترجيح بزيادة العدالة لأن الترجيح يقع بكثرة العلل حتى لا يترجح القياس بقياس آخر ولا الحديث بحديث آخر، وشهادة كل شاهدين علة تامة فلا تصلح للترجيح والعدالة ليست بذي حد فلا يقع الترجيح بها .
His statement: (A house) in the hand of another, a man claimed half of it and another claimed all of it, and they presented evidence, then for the first is one quarter and the rest is for the other according to Abu Hanifa, considering the method of opposition: the one claiming half does not contest the other regarding half, so it is surrendered to him, and their opposition is equal in the other half, so it is divided equally between them. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is divided into thirds between them, considering the method of 'awl and mudaraba: the one claiming all enters with his full right (two shares) and the one claiming half enters with one share, so it is divided into thirds. الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preference; in this context, giving weight to one evidence over another.

Eight Cases of 'Awl and the Munaza'a Dispute
Enumerating division cases by method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of division cases in Hanafi fiqh and identify which cases are settled by 'awl and which by munaza'a, including the intra-school disagreement.

Core Idea
Eight cases use 'awl unanimously; one uses munaza'a; three split between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes Qadikhan's classification of all division cases according to method. Understanding this enumeration is essential for any mufti or judge dealing with conflicting claims in inheritance, debts, bequests, or crimes. The key distinction is between proportional reduction ('awl) and contested allocation (munaza'a).

Guided Path
1
Grasp the four overarching categories
Qadikhan divides all division issues into four types: (1) those divided by 'awl unanimously, (2) those by munaza'a unanimously, (3) those where Abu Hanifa uses munaza'a and the Sahibayn use 'awl, and (4) those where the opposite applies.
The passage details types 1-3; type 4 is mentioned but not elaborated.
2
Memorize the eight unanimous 'awl cases
Eight specific scenarios are listed: inheritance insufficient for shares, diverse debts, multiple bequests exceeding one-third, bequest with favoritism, bequest of manumission, bequest of absolute sums, a slave committing two crimes, a mudabbar's crime.
These cases all involve a shortage such that no claimant can take his full due, requiring proportional reduction.
3
Understand the single unanimous munaza'a case
The only case where munaza'a is used by all is when two fuduli sellers sell the same slave (whole and half) and the owner ratifies both. The method gives the whole-buyer 3/4 and the half-buyer 1/4.
Munaza'a means each takes his uncontested portion (here the half-buyer's uncontested half is contested with the whole), then the remaining contested portion is divided equally.
4
Analyze the three disputed cases
In these, Abu Hanifa applies munaza'a while the Sahibayn apply 'awl. The first example: two claimants to a house (whole vs. half) both have evidence. Abu Hanifa gives 3/4 to the whole-claimant and 1/4 to the half-claimant; the Sahibayn would use 'awl (proportional reduction) based on the amounts claimed.
The passage only gives the first disputed case; the other two are not enumerated but fall under the same ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختصر الشارح مسائلها وقال : وبيان طرق هذه المسائل وتخريجها على هذه الأصول وتمام تفريعها مذكور في شرح الزيادات لقاضيخان .اهـ. وقد يسر الله تعالى لي بشرح الزيادات لقاضيخان قبيل تأليف هذا المحل فأحببت أن أنقلها منه بألفاظه فأقول مستعيناً بالله قال قاضيخان في هذا الشرح من كتاب الجنايات من باب جناية أم الولد على مولاها وعلى غيره وجنس مسائل القسمة أربع، منها ما يقسم بطريق العول والمضاربة عند الكل، ومنها ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عندهم، ومنها ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما بطريق العول والمضاربة، ومنها ما يقسم على عكس ذلك. أما ما يقسم بطريق العول عندهم ثمانٍ : إحداها الميراث إذا اجتمعت سهام الفرائض في التركة وضاقت التركة عن الوفاء بها تقسم التركة بين أرباب الديون على طريق العول. والثانية إذا اجتمعت الديون المتفاوتة وضاقت التركة عن الوفاء بها تقسم التركة بين أرباب الديون بطريق العول. والثالثة إذا أوصى لرجل بثلث ماله ولآخر ماله ولآخر بربع بسدس ماله ولم تجز الورثة حتى عادت الوصايا إلى الثلث يقسم الثلث بينهم على طريق العول. والرابعة الوصية بالمحاباة إذا أوصى أن يباع العبد الذي قيمته ثلاثة آلاف درهم من هذا الرجل بألفي درهم وأوصى لآخر أن يباع منه العبد الذي يساوي ألفي درهم بألف درهم حتى حصلت المحاباة لهما بألفي درهم كان الثلث بينهما بطريق العول. والخامسة الوصية بالعتق إذا أوصى بأن يعتق من هذا العبد نصفه وأوصى بأن يعتق من هذا الآخر ثلثه وذاك لا يخرج من الثلث يقسم ثلث المال بينهما بطريق العول ويسقط من كل واحد منهما حصته من السعاية والسادسة الوصية بألف مرسلة إذا أوصى لرجل بألف ولآخر بألفين كان الثلث بينهما بطريق العول والسابعة عبد فقأ عين رجل وقتل آخر خطأ فدفع بهما يقسم الجاني بينهما بطريق العول ثلثاه لولي القتيل وثلثه للآخر . والثامنة مدبر جنى على هذا الوجه ودفعت القيمة إلى أولياء الجناية كانت القيمة بينهما بطريق العول. وأما ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عندهم مسألة واحدة ذكرها في جامع الفصولين : فضولي باع عبداً من رجل بألف درهم وفضولي آخر باع نصفه من آخر بخمسمائة فأجاز المولى البيعين جميعاً يخير المشتريان، فإن اختارا الأخذ أخذاً بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعه لمشتري الكل وربعه لمشتري النصف جميعاً . عندهم وأما ما يقسم بطريق المنازعة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما بطريق العول ثلاث مسائل : إحداها دار تنازع فيها رجلان أحدهما يدعي كلها والآخر يدعي نصفها وأقاما البينة عند أبي حنيفة تقسم الدار بينهما بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعها لمدعي الكل والربع لمدعي النصف،
And the commentator summarized its issues and said: The explanation of the ways of these issues, their derivation from these principles, and the complete details of their subdivisions are mentioned in Sharh al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan. God facilitated for me the explanation of Sharh al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan shortly before composing this place, so I desired to quote it from him in his words. I say, seeking God's help: Qadikhan said in this commentary, from the Book of Crimes, chapter on the crime of Umm al-Walad against her master and others: The categories of division issues are four: those that are divided by the way of 'awl and mudaraba according to all; those that are divided by the way of munaza'a according to them; those that are divided by the way of munaza'a according to Abu Hanifa but according to the two by the way of 'awl and mudaraba; and those that are divided in the opposite manner. As for those divided by the way of 'awl according to all, there are eight: First, inheritance when the obligatory shares in the estate come together and the estate is insufficient to fulfill them; the estate is divided among the entitled parties by 'awl. Second, when diverse debts come together and the estate is insufficient to fulfill them; the estate is divided among the creditors by 'awl. Third, when a person bequeaths to a man a third of his wealth, to another his wealth, to another a quarter, to another a sixth, and the heirs do not permit it until the bequests are reduced to the third; the third is divided among them by 'awl. Fourth, bequest with favoritism (muhabah) when one bequeaths that a slave worth three thousand dirhams be sold to this man for two thousand, and bequeaths to another that a slave worth two thousand be sold to him for one thousand, so the favoritism total is two thousand; the third (of the estate) is divided between them by 'awl. Fifth, bequest of manumission when one bequeaths that half of this slave be freed and another bequeaths that one third of that other slave be freed, and that cannot be taken from the third; the third of the wealth is divided between them by 'awl, and each one drops his share of the earning (sa'ayah). Sixth, bequest of a specific thousand, if he bequeaths a thousand to a man and two thousand to another; the third is divided between them by 'awl. Seventh, a slave gouged out a man's eye and killed another by mistake, and is handed over for both; the perpetrator is divided between them by 'awl: two thirds to the heir of the slain and one third to the other. Eighth, a mudabbar (slave whose freedom is deferred) committed a crime in this manner and the value is paid to the claimants; the value is divided between them by 'awl. As for what is divided by the way of munaza'a according to them, there is one issue mentioned in Jami' al-Fuslain: A fuduli (unauthorized agent) sold a slave to a man for a thousand dirhams, and another fuduli sold half of it to another for five hundred; the master permits both sales. The two buyers have the option: if they choose to take, they take by the way of munaza'a: three quarters for the buyer of the whole and one quarter for the buyer of the half, according to them. As for what is divided by the way of munaza'a according to Abu Hanifa but according to the two by the way of 'awl, there are three issues: First, a house about which two men dispute, one claiming the whole and the other claiming half, and they present evidence; according to Abu Hanifa, the house is divided between them by munaza'a: three quarters for the claimant of the whole and one quarter for the claimant of the half.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a classification of all division cases according to the methods of 'awl (proportional reduction) and munaza'a (opposition), as derived from Qadikhan's commentary. It begins by stating that the commentator (of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) summarizes the points and defers details to Sharh al-Ziyadat. Then he quotes Qadikhan: the genus of division issues is four types: (1) those divided by 'awl unanimously (eight cases), (2) those divided by munaza'a unanimously (one case), (3) those where Abu Hanifa uses munaza'a and the Sahibayn use 'awl (three cases), and (4) those where the opposite applies (not detailed here). The eight 'awl cases cover inheritance with insufficient funds, debts, bequests, manumission, and crimes by slaves. The one munaza'a case involves a fuduli sale of a slave. The three cases of ikhtilaf include the house case already discussed, and presumably two others (not fully listed here due to page break). This classification demonstrates the systematic approach of Hanafi fiqh in resolving conflicting claims.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total exceeds the whole; used in inheritance and debts.
المنازعة (al-munaza'a): A division method where each claimant takes his uncontested portion, then the contested remains are divided equally.
المضاربة (al-mudaraba): Partnership; here used as a proportional division method based on the amounts of claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many cases are divided unanimously by the way of 'awl according to Qadikhan's classification?
A) Three
B) Eight
C) One
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh classifies division cases into four categories based on whether the method is 'awl or munaza'a, with three disputed cases where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ.
